Shen Bao Children's Special

Soldiers Defending the Nation 174

— Qian Zhongzheng

Boom! Boom! Boom! The sounds of cannons have shattered the god of peace; Clap! Clap! Clap! The sounds of gunfire have broken the sweet dreams of humanity; such a terrifying scene is enough to make people tremble.

Suddenly, a signal cannon is heard, and the entire team rushes forward like flying. Along the roads and paths they pass, "crimson blood flies," and "righteous spirit fills the air." What are they fighting for? For whom do they shed their heads and spill their hot blood?

They fight for justice, they fight for the survival of our nation, unwilling to succumb. Therefore, they are willing to sacrifice everything—bidding farewell to their parents, leaving their siblings, and going to the battlefield to fight to the death!

Soldiers on the front lines! I hope you work hard! Strive forward!

Take your guns and overthrow this power and tyranny. Ahead is the wide road to eternal happiness. May you bravely pass through it. I am willing to advance, treading on your bloodstains! Although there are thousands of miles of thorns ahead, as long as we have a spirit of fearlessness, we can forge a path!

The Story of a French Little Boy 175

— Jiang Yin

In 1868, during the Franco-Prussian War, when news of the Prussian army's impending attack on Paris reached France, the French people felt extremely indignant and apprehensive. At this time, a young boy left his hometown and came to the military camp.

"What is your name?" an officer asked him.

"La Chennei, General!" he replied.

"Why did you become a soldier at such a young age?"

"Because I want to save this endangered motherland."

"..."

Later, he resolutely took on a very difficult and dangerous task that others dared not undertake—reconnoitering the enemy's situation—disguising himself as a deaf-mute, with a few pieces of bread and a short flute in his pocket, he left his army.

Unfortunately, he was captured by the enemy and watched by four fierce soldiers, leaving him no chance to escape.

When La Chennei was tied to a field camp by the Prussian soldiers, preparing to carry out the death penalty, he felt the terror of death for the first time; although his heart was splitting like cells dividing one by one, he showed no fear on the surface.

The Prussian officer sternly asked him if he was a French military scout. He just shook his head, as if saying, "I am a deaf-mute. I can't hear your words, nor can I understand your words." Then he took out the flute from his pocket and calmly began to play the score. In this way, he was finally released as a deaf-mute.

He escaped from the tiger's mouth back to his own camp, detailing the enemy's situation. As a result, Paris was able to turn danger into safety.

Dear children: What do you think of this story after hearing it? At that time, the French child La Chennei not only had great courage but also great wisdom. As a result, France finally relied on him to achieve its final survival. His contribution to the motherland was so great!

Children: The dangerous and serious situation of our country, China, at present, may be one day like the French situation during the Franco-Prussian War. At that time, I don't expect every child to achieve La Chennei's great career. However, in the end, I must offer the children some advice to make a practical preparation for you. Because no matter what you do, you must have sufficient preparation.

The Wild Goose 176

— Chen Jianju

Looking up at the sky,

A flock of geese flies north.

Geese!

Did you perhaps hear some news from the north,

Such a hurry!

Such tension!

Braving the wind and frost,

Forming a "one" and "person" formation,

Like preparing to join the battle.

But…

Geese!

Please tell me,

The situation in the north,

Is it safe and sound?

The Three States of Matter 177

— Zhen

One day, Min'er sat alone, blankly, silently thinking, feeling that this world was too wonderful.

"Min-di, what are you doing sitting blankly? Are you feeling unwell?" Cong'er, seeing his younger brother sitting blankly for a long time, asked him this way.

"No, I feel very comfortable. I'm just thinking, feeling that this world is too mysterious."

"Eh, what's mysterious? You think it's mysterious, where is it mysterious?"

"Look, in my surroundings, there isn't a single thing that's the same. That's a tank of clear water, that's a table. Don't you think it's mysterious?"

"What's mysterious? Water is a liquid, a table is a solid, of course they won't be the same."

"Brother, I want to ask you, what is a solid, what is a liquid? What's the difference?"

"All matter is divided into three states: (1) Solid: A solid has a definite shape and volume. What is a definite shape? It means that its shape will not change. For example, a table always has the same shape, and you never see today's table being square and tomorrow turning round. (2) Liquid: A liquid has a definite volume, but its shape changes with the container that holds it. What is a definite volume? For example, if you want to put a basin of water into a teacup, then this teacup will definitely not be able to hold the basin of water, and it will spill out of the cup. This is all because its volume is definite. However, its shape is ever-changing. (3) Gas: A gas has no definite shape or volume, it is the most wonderful. We cannot see it, so of course we cannot know its shape and volume. But in nature, there is an even stranger thing, which is that there is a kind of liquid that can become a solid and a gas, but it can also change back from a solid and a gas to its original state. Do you know what it is?"

"That liquid is water. It can be said to be the most important thing in the world, and also the most wonderful. Water is a kind of liquid, that's something everyone knows. If it encounters heat, it will turn into water vapor, and this water vapor is a gas. But if water vapor encounters cold, it will turn into rainwater, which is a liquid transformed from water vapor. If water encounters cold, it will condense into ice, and ice is a solid. But if ice encounters heat, part of it will turn into water vapor, and part of it will turn into water. Such a cycle is a very strange thing, but other things will not cycle in this way."

Becoming a Chrysanthemum 178

— Chen Tiewu

Ming'er visited the chrysanthemum exhibition with his father and said to his father, "Dad! Please buy a few pots to take back. It would be interesting to display them at home during the New Year!" His father said, "Silly child! It's getting cold. The chrysanthemums are going to wither, how can they last until the New Year?" Ming'er asked again, "Is there a way to keep them from withering?" His father stroked his beard and said, "Yes, there is. I'll tell you when we get home."

Ming'er's father, took Ming'er, passed a paper store, and his father bought a sheet of white Hanglian paper and a sheet of yellow paper. Then, he bought two chi of thin lead wire at a sundries store. He said to Ming'er, "I'll make a chrysanthemum when we get home, just like the ones you just saw, and it will never wither."

When his father got home, he folded the white paper several times and sewed it tightly in the middle (as shown in Figure 1). Then he took a small bowl—a compass would be better—placed it upside down on the folded paper, drew a circle around the small bowl with a pencil, and cut off the unused parts (as shown in Figure 2). Next, he divided the circular white paper into several equal parts with a pencil, forming chrysanthemum petal shapes, and cut them open with scissors (as shown in Figure 3). Then, he placed the cut petals on his lap, used an awl, placed the tip of the awl at the tip of the petal, and pulled it back forcefully. The petals would curl up, just like real petals (as shown in Figure 4). After all the petals were made, he peeled off the white paper one by one and glued them to the made flower center with paste (as shown in Figure 5). This created a chrysanthemum.

(The method for making the flower center is very simple, just fold the yellow paper several times, tie the lower part with lead wire, and cut the upper part into thin threads with scissors.)

He made the chrysanthemum and asked Ming'er, "Does it look like a real chrysanthemum?" Ming'er said, "It looks just like one." Ming'er then asked, "The white chrysanthemum is made like this, what about the red chrysanthemum? What about the yellow chrysanthemum?..." His father said, "That's easy. To make colored chrysanthemums, just apply the required color to the white paper before folding it."

Children: Do you like chrysanthemums? If you have time, it would be nice to make one to play with, wouldn't it?

Methods of Protection Against Poison Gas 180

— Zhiyuan

Our China is now suffering from a very severe invasion by the enemy. Soon we will have to go all out to resist them, and there will be a great war. In this war, the most terrible thing is the enemy's release of poison gas. If we inhale this poison gas, we will be injured if it is light, and we will lose our lives if it is heavy, and life will be very dangerous. Therefore, we should now have some common sense about poison gas protection, so that in future wars, if the enemy releases poison gas, we can take precautions to avoid harm.

Below are some common sense about poison gas protection. I hope that after everyone knows it, they will tell others about it.

When a poison gas bomb bursts, the sound is very small, and a lot of smoke or liquid flows out, and there is a special stench. When we encounter this situation, we can know that the enemy is releasing poison gas.

At this time, we must calm down and think about ways to defend ourselves; we must not panic and run around, because this is not helpful, and because the heart beats fast and breathing is rapid, the result is that a lot of poison gas is inhaled.

At home, we must first prepare things such as felt cotton curtains. When poison gas is released, immediately seal the windows and doors tightly to prevent poison gas from entering. It would be even better if a tightly sealed gas-proof room could be equipped. The food at home should be covered with airtight food covers, and the water well should be covered to prevent contamination.

If you want to escape from poison gas, you must pay attention to the wind direction and walk on the road that is at right angles to the wind direction. For example, if a westerly wind is blowing, you should run north or south, not east, because if you go with the wind, the poison gas will always be behind you, and you will never escape.

Also, it must be known that poison gas is heavier than air, so the poison gas is thicker in low places. Places such as fields, forests, and valleys are not to be visited. It is best to escape to a poison gas shelter, run upstairs, and close the windows tightly, which can reduce the amount of poison you are exposed to.

In advance, everyone should prepare two gas masks. When poison gas is released, put on the gas mask to avoid poison. If there is no gas mask, then you can cover your mouth and nose with a towel or handkerchief soaked in soapy water or urine, or take a bamboo tube filled with mud, soak it in urine, and attach it to your mouth and nose for breathing, and immediately escape to a high place or mountain where there is no poison gas.

If you have already been poisoned by poison gas, then quickly move to a place with fresh air, carefully take off your clothes, rinse your whole body with hot water, try to maintain your body temperature, drink some boiled water, tea or coffee, and then ask a doctor to treat you according to the nature of the poison gas. If you have been exposed to corrosive poison gas, then quickly wash your whole body with a bleach solution. People who have been poisoned should be quiet and should not move or scratch around, or excite their bodies, so as not to trigger the poison and increase the degree of harm.

Children, Arise! 181

— Big Kid

——A Letter to Children Nationwide

Dear Children:

I often communicate with you, but I haven't had the opportunity. Now, because there are many things I must discuss with you, I am borrowing a corner of this garden to write you this open letter.

At present, our country has reached the era of storms, and our national crisis has reached its final moment. If we still have humanity, if we are unwilling to be slaves of a conquered nation, we can only shoulder our responsibilities and rise up to save ourselves. Especially children, you should no longer hide in the arms of your parents and enjoy happiness, you should no longer be pampered and act as willful young ladies and gentlemen, because you are the cornerstone of the nation, the future masters of the country. For the sake of the country and the nation, you must train yourselves and encourage others to become patriotic and enthusiastic comrades.

In recent days, the pseudo-bandits have invaded Suiyuan, and the whole country is indignant. Fortunately, the generals guarding the territory in front and the enthusiastic soldiers on the border have risen up to resist the enemy. Now the heroes on the front line are fighting bloody battles in the icy and snowy weather, in the midst of artillery fire and smoke. They have forgotten their own lives, forgotten the cold on their bodies, and are only fighting and sacrificing for the sake of the motherland's mountains and rivers and the survival of the entire nation. But, dear children, how should we admire and respect those national heroes?

Recently, all parts of the country have launched a campaign to aid Suiyuan and to comfort the soldiers on the front lines; we only need to open the newspaper every day to see the automatic and enthusiastic donations from all walks of life, from adults and gentlemen to vendors and peddlers, as much as hundreds of thousands and as little as a dime. Some are even launching what are called one-day movements, dime movements, one-week movements, and fasting movements. This shows that our nation is indeed much more awake than in the past. Although these so-called movements may be a bit contrived, their patriotic enthusiasm is still commendable.

Although we are still young and cannot talk about dying on the battlefield, our patriotic enthusiasm comes from innocence and is no weaker than that of adults. Moreover, the loyalty and bravery of the soldiers on the front lines still require the support and encouragement of the people in the rear. I now hope that the children of the whole country will unite to aid Suiyuan, accumulate the expenses of games, toys, sweets, etc. on weekdays, or purchase necessary comfort items, and send them to the newspaper groups to transport them to the front lines, and at any time persuade classmates, companions, parents and relatives to donate; I believe that as long as you are willing to do this, the results must be very impressive!

Now is the time to roar; children, arise! Arise!

Young Pioneer Mailbox

Letters That Others Cannot See 182

——Reply to Chen Huimin of Nanjing

Brother Huimin:

You told us about the scene of practicing tracking at the foot of Zijin Mountain. We thought about it carefully and felt that the reason for your failure was not as you imagined, because your team members took the wrong path. Because in any case, we think that not every team member would have entered the wrong path in this way.

According to our speculation: It must be that the secret letter you hid under the tree was discovered by the members of your friend team. Since they knew your secret, they changed the guiding signs you had prepared in advance, and of course the result was that your team members all took the wrong path. I wonder what you think of our speculation?

But whether our speculation is correct or not, you must design it more carefully when you practice tracking next time. Just talking about your secret letter, no matter how you place it there, you must find a way to give the team members a hint, usually by drawing a sign for hiding the letter in a conspicuous place. But you don't necessarily have to do this. As long as you and the team members agree in advance, the sign for hiding the letter may be changed to another method. Clever Young Pioneers will often secretly replace the "advance sign" with the "stop sign", and replace the "stop sign" with the "advance sign"! Also, you can tell the team members in advance that there may be a hidden letter at the roundabout, big tree or big rock, so your sign for hiding the letter does not need to be written in a conspicuous place: As for the newly built content, why do you need to write it out clearly? Have you forgotten the wonderful methods of secret communication? Every Young Pioneer should know at least three kinds of secret communication methods. I will give you a simple example here:

First, find a long and narrow strip of paper, for example, cut out the blank edge of the white paper, roll it diagonally along the Young Pioneer's army stick, and then write the words you want to write on it, writing vertically or horizontally is up to you. Then, when you take it off after writing, there will only be fragmented strokes or meaningless words on the paper strip. When your team member receives this paper strip and rolls it on the army stick in the same way, won't he understand the secret of the long strip of paper? But one thing to note is that the paper strip should be as narrow as possible.

This is just an example. You should of course use it as a basis to invent more methods. But no matter what method is good, as long as both of you know it, it will be ineffective if others know it.

I hope that your next tracking can achieve satisfactory results; I also hope to report to us again. Please, I wish you

Effort!

China Young Pioneer Self-Help Society respectfully replies

Deep Sea Dream Travels 183

— Written by Jiangzhong Yu

(Seven) When Min'er arrived at the bottom of the sea, he saw many strange and beautiful plants. (Eight) He walked and played at the bottom of the sea, and small fish swam by his side one by one. He felt very excited and forgot that he was at the bottom of the sea. (Nine) After a while, a group of very beautiful fish swam in front of him. (Ten) The fish looked like American freshwater fin fish, with yellow and black patterns on their bodies. (Eleven) He was enjoying watching, when suddenly a cloud of black water came from behind. He turned around and saw that it was a huge squid.

Filial Piety (6) 184

— Hai

Bertha Koskov lay there trembling for a while. Finally, she heard the two of them snoring loudly, knowing that they were asleep. So she fell asleep soundly too, until after the sun was shining brightly, she was awakened by the old woman. The two of them actually prepared a very rich breakfast for her, and they spoke to her much more gently, asking her a lot of questions, but she only told them half of her story. The two of them listened quietly, seeming very interested, and even stated that they had searched her last night because they suspected she was a dishonest vagrant, and did not want to rob her money. Bertha Koskov happily left their house; but when she opened her money bag, she saw that the eighty copper Kopeks had turned into one hundred and twenty. She firmly believed that their original intention was indeed to rob her money, and that it was thanks to God somehow inspiring them to have good intentions, and instead helping her. In addition, she suffered a great fright. One day early in the morning, she was walking out from where she had stayed the night, and everyone else had not yet gotten up. She was the only one walking on the street. All the dogs in the village chased after her. She ran, hitting them desperately with her cane, but the more she hit them, the angrier they became. One of the dogs grabbed her skirt, causing her to fall to the ground, and she suddenly felt a cold nose against the back of her neck; but the dog sniffed her, and did not even bite her. At this time, a farmer happened to pass by and drove all the dogs away.

Severe winter had arrived, and it had snowed heavily for eight consecutive days, forcing her to stay. But when she was preparing to set off again, the farmers busily told her that if she were to walk alone in such a large snowdrift, even the strongest man would lose his life, because the wind would roll up the snow on the ground, making it impossible to distinguish the road, and it would be very dangerous to walk through. Therefore, they kept her, waiting for a team of snow carts to arrive, which were carrying food to Igasarininburg to supply the Christmas banquet. The drivers of those snow carts listened to her story and were willing to let her sit in their carts, but her clothes were very thin and not suitable for winter travel. Although they had unloaded the wrapping cloth from their goods and wrapped it around her, on the fourth day at a desolate post station, she could not bear the attack of the severe cold, and one of her cheeks was already frostbitten. They had to take her off the snow cart and rub her cheeks with snow to prevent frostbite, and they were very concerned about her. They all said that without a sheepskin coat, they could not take her forward, because the farther they went, the colder it would be, and she would definitely be frozen to death. Bertha Koskov thought that she could no longer travel with these kind-hearted people, and that the post station might not be able to keep her, which put her in a dilemma, and she could not help but cry sadly. The drivers, seeing that she was very pitiful, agreed to pool some money to buy her a sheepskin coat, but there was no place to buy one; the people at the post station could not give up their coats either, because this was a very remote place, and it was really not easy to buy another coat. Although the drivers had tried to negotiate with the waitress in the hotel at a particularly high price, possibly selling her coat, she also refused.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Book and Newspaper Chronicles

Review of Gu Jiegang's Edited "Popular Knowledge" 185

— Zhang Ziliang

——Price per issue: 16 cents. Sole distributor: Shanghai Yadong Library——

"Popular Knowledge" is edited by Mr. Gu Jiegang, which I believe is already known to the readers. My overall impression of this publication is relatively positive, and I feel that it is one of the more readable periodicals available today. However, to truly critique it, it also has its shortcomings. Let's examine the recently published third issue.

Generally speaking, this issue of "Popular Knowledge," like the previous two, still lacks richness in content. For example, philosophy, social sciences, literary theory, and international politics and economics are not prominently featured, or even completely absent, in this issue of "Popular Knowledge." However, these are precisely the "knowledge" that the "masses" urgently demand. Of course, the space of a semi-monthly publication is limited, and it cannot include all "knowledge." However, under the current circumstances, a publication that claims to be "Popular Knowledge" should have philosophy as the foundation of all theories, as well as international politics and economics that are closely related to everyone's real lives. "Popular Knowledge" emphasizes introductions to the lives and character of famous figures in ancient China and devotes a large amount of space to publishing articles of the "casual talk" and "essay" type. This cannot be said to be completely wrong, but comparatively, I believe that instead of using so much space to publish these things, it would be better to collect more of the aforementioned more important knowledge to enrich the content of the publication.

This issue of "Popular Knowledge" contains four quite serious essays: The first is Mr. Wu Shichang's "On the Trend of Higher Education Emphasizing Science and Engineering." This article offers very appropriate criticisms of the opinions of those who "emphasize science and engineering" education and despise the humanities and law disciplines, and of the shallow views that only value technology and disregard theory. The author also clearly points out that "it is not a national disgrace if a country unfortunately lags behind in technology and needs to import talent from other countries"; "However, if a country's fundamental plan is handled and decided without great vision, resulting in a mess and forcing it to listen to the interference and coercion of 'friendly nations' or other countries, that is a great shame and disgrace, and a fatal disease of national subjugation." Finally, it concludes that "we should now (1) start by promoting academic thought, to (2) cultivate a scientific spirit, attitude, and method—rather than a narrow type of technology." These are all undeniable in principle. However, when Mr. Wu criticizes those shallow views, he only engages in theoretical debates and does not fundamentally point out the social intentions of those "emphasizing science and engineering" technocrats who are planning for the interests of a minority, preventing readers from more deeply understanding why they would adopt such methods. Moreover, even in the theoretical criticism, in some places, he still reveals the backwardness of his own fundamental stance, such as his absolute endorsement of Kant without knowing the errors of his agnosticism. At the same time, what is even more puzzling is that in expressing his opinions on Chinese higher education based on general theory and China's actual situation, and in demonstrating the positive role of education for the country and society, Mr. Wu suddenly put forward the proposition of "learning for the sake of learning," saying it is "the most precious spirit in learning." If this proposition is correct, then students need not think about the country and nation when studying, and educators need not think about the role of education, making Mr. Wu's educational opinions superfluous. In my opinion, Mr. Wu confuses the utilitarianism of learning, the theory of "applying what one has learned," and the tendency to "treat learning only as a stepping stone." Therefore, he praises the spirit of "learning for the sake of learning." We believe that it is indeed wrong to study for the sake of becoming an official and getting rich, but "applying what one has learned" is a correct proposition. It is perfectly acceptable to encourage students to concentrate on research, but advocating "learning for the sake of learning" is unacceptable, because the latter implies that people should study in isolation from reality, "building a cart behind closed doors." In fact, science and engineering are naturally very practical, and even the humanities and law disciplines are very useful, isn't this something that even Mr. Wu admits? Therefore, the so-called spirit of "learning for the sake of learning" is entirely nonsense. The second is Mr. Zhu Baochang's "United Front in National Crisis," and the third is Mr. Lian Shisheng's "Overproduction and Underconsumption." We have no other opinions on these two articles except to say that the content is lacking in richness. Finally, there is Mr. Gu Jiegang's

Page 18

"Sacrifice." In this essay, Mr. Gu asks everyone to sacrifice for national liberation, to sacrifice the individual "small self" for the survival of the race's "big self." This is indeed a very correct proposition at present. However, in my opinion, due to the continuous attacks of the enemy, the interests of various groups of people in China and the interests of the entire nation have more or less converged. Therefore, we should not only awaken the people to sacrifice the individual for the nation, but also awaken them to rise up and save themselves. Saving the country and saving oneself are one and the same issue at present and do not conflict. We should unite to save the country and save ourselves. Awakening the general public in this way will achieve greater results. At the same time, Mr. Gu also said at the beginning of the article: "Maintaining one's own survival and possessing one's own private property are two basic desires of mankind, which everyone has. All phenomena of human survival, evolution, and development are derived and sublimated from these two desires." We believe that this cannot become a general absolute judgment because, in a certain stage of historical development, mankind did not have "private property," and therefore had no desire for private ownership. In fact, aren't there countries in the world now that have no desire for private ownership? Yet no one can say that those countries are not "evolving." Therefore, although Mr. Gu's proposition is correct in China at present, the basic theoretical arguments still deserve further study.

There are two current affairs commentaries: namely, "The Long-Term Negotiations Between China and Japan" and "Roosevelt's Re-election as US President." We have no differing opinions on the former and can skip it. As for the latter, it only explains that Landon's "conservative thinking" and his closeness to the coalition party of Lemke and Coughlin were the reasons for his failure. It only superficially introduces the general policies implemented by Roosevelt and does not more deeply point out the groups of people represented by the American Republican and Democratic parties and the essence of the policies they implement in the election competition. At the same time, the article does not provide any analysis of the impact of Roosevelt's re-election on the United States and the world. Strictly speaking, this is very inadequate.

One of the main features of "Popular Knowledge" is its fondness for publishing biographies of ancient people. Their intention is nothing more than to teach people today by describing the character and lives of certain ancient people, which is certainly not to be criticized. However, when we rewrite about ancient people, we should not only talk about their family environment and private lives but also explain all their expressions from their social environment. Because in this way, readers can have a deeper understanding of ancient people and history and can receive more powerful lessons. However, this publication is not like that. For example, Mr. Zheng Kankan's "Wang Anshi" in this issue only explains Wang Anshi's achievements based on his family environment and his nature and simply attributes the reasons for Anshi's failure to his "not humiliating himself," "being good at self-preservation," and "not cooperating with others." This can be said to be a completely individualistic view. We ask: If Wang lived in the Shang and Zhou dynasties, could he "implement reforms"? If commercial capital in the Song dynasty had defeated the feudal landlords, would there be any fault to find with Anshi's "not humiliating himself," "being good at self-preservation," and "not cooperating with others"? This is probably difficult for the author of the article to answer. Another example is Mr. Wang Chongwu's "Hoelun" (Genghis Khan Temujin's mother), which also simply attributes Temujin's achievements to his mother's teaching. From the author's intention, it is to have mothers now learn from Hoelun and teach us a few Temujins. This cannot be said to be wrong, but to rely on mother's education to revive the nation, to have women all become Hoelun, is to exaggerate the subject too much, exaggerating it to the point of being wrong.

Mr. Shen Congwen's "The Significance of the Literary World's United Front" asks people to be "tolerant" on one hand, but on the other hand, it firmly adheres to history, saying how the past was like this and how the past was like that, which seems a bit unfair, although Mr. Shen's basic stance is consistent with everyone's. Mr. Lu Zheyi's novel "Eyes" is a work rich in national liberation consciousness, but the descriptive techniques cannot be said to be refined; some places are even "speeding." Mr. Tian Tao's novel, "Heat," is an even more immature creation. Not only does the content lack positive meaning, but the structure of the writing and the organization of the story are also very loose.

Finally, we hope that people will regard this criticism as well-intentioned, and we hope that "Popular Knowledge" can continuously enrich its content, continue to improve, and become a very progressive publication. We also love to read some of the writings and theories in "Popular Knowledge," so we put forward the above opinions, hoping that Mr. Gu can edit it even better.

Humorous Sketch

The Barber's Curse 186

— Pei Ming

I can assume that every discerning person will agree with me that one of the most hateful things in a person's life is a haircut. Every week, or at most every two weeks, you have to endure this almost prescribed punishment. For as long as you live in this so-called civilized world, you have to endure this punishment. Of course, the hair of savages grows so long, but in this modern era, everything must be "streamlined" and maintain a popular style, so you have to consider your appearance. For this reason, one has reason to envy the cleverness of the Indian Sikh, who hides his messy hair under his colorful turban and lets his beard make his face ugly, without bothering himself with weekly haircuts and daily shaves. In this way, how much time and trouble can be saved, and should we learn from their example?

I hate going to the barbershop. First, you have to wait for your turn. A good barbershop is often crowded with customers. Sometimes, this wait may continue for as long as half an hour. Then, when it's your turn, you have to sit motionless in a special chair (the design of this chair is for the convenience of the barber and less for the comfort of the customer), for a time that ranges from half an hour to an hour, all depending on the barber's skill. During this time, all your freedom is lost. You have to obediently and quickly follow his commands, turning your head this way and that way, and often even conforming to his arbitrary arrangements.

Barbers seem to be mostly unkind. They cut your hair and shave your face with the same carelessness as peeling sweet potatoes. They grab your head with great force, as if afraid you're going to slip out of their hands. They use so many fancy techniques with scissors and razors that you can't help but shiver at the sight. They also shake your head frequently, and before half of the haircut is done, you're already dizzy. Yet you have to endure this pain without protest, for fear that an angry barber will deliberately harm your noble head.

In addition to being bound to the chair without any freedom of movement and the many sufferings you endure, you also have the fear of what parts of your face the barber's scissors and razors will cut off. This fear is not entirely unfounded, because you can't expect the barber to be clear-headed all day long. He may have drunk too much wine or be indulging in the pleasure of daydreaming while working, or he may have lost interest and attention in his monotonous barbering work. Any of these situations can make him forget the work in his hands and the sacredness of your head. Therefore, every time I decide to leave the barbershop, I always carefully and tightly hold my head in front of the mirror to check whether I have lost anything before paying.

I heard that a famous general always had four guards holding pistols to protect him when he got a haircut, for fear that the barber was colluding with his political enemies. With just a flick of that sharp razor, his throat could be cut. In addition, we also heard that this general always chose a new barber every time he needed a haircut, so that his political enemies would not have the opportunity to assassinate him through the barber. This example shows how a general should take precautions when getting a haircut. Undoubtedly, we civilians don't have to worry about someone colluding with the barber to harm us, but we still can't be at ease, because who can say that the barber won't accidentally cut something off your face?

I often think that if someone could invent a machine that could use its own hands to cut one's hair into any style within five minutes, how beneficial would that be to humanity. We are talking about saving time and energy. I wonder why someone doesn't apply their genius to the invention of a haircutting machine that saves time and energy. Given the fact that complicated machines are invented from time to time, I don't believe that it is completely impossible to invent such a haircutting machine. Some inventions do improve people's fate, but if we still have to endure the punishment of haircuts from time to time, then we still can't say that our life is a happy life.

Some people argue that haircutting is the most suitable time to evoke your most pleasant imaginations, because at this time, no one will come to disturb and stop your train of thought. I have tried this argument many times, but found that the atmosphere inside is not suitable for imagining anything. When scissors and razors dance all over your face, all that is evoked are terrible thoughts. When your heart is overcome with terror, you naturally cannot think of anything sweet and happy.

Others suggest that you concentrate on reading the tabloid's gossip news to reduce the aversion to haircuts. Undoubtedly, this is a good suggestion, but for people with impaired vision like me, I can hardly read anything without glasses, and whenever I get a haircut, the barber always insists on taking off my glasses before starting.

Some people also suggest that when the barber is giving you a haircut, you can close your eyes and take a nap. Indeed, it is common to see a few customers napping in the barbershop. Although I also like to take a nap very much, I dare not completely entrust my head to the barber's care. I would rather stay awake so that if anything goes wrong with my head, I can notice it without being unaware. In addition, drowsiness is contagious. If I fall asleep, the barber cannot resist my influence, and then you can easily imagine what a terrible result that would be. Furthermore, barbershops nowadays have both male and female customers. The barber is not a person without emotions. When he is cutting your hair, he may often cast his gaze at your beautiful neighbor to satisfy his hungry eyes. In this situation, the danger to your head is doubled. Therefore, I think it is both cautious and smart not to nap in the barbershop.

After lamenting the many inconveniences and pains of haircuts, sometimes I have no choice but to look at bald people with envy. However, strangely, when a person discovers that his hair is thinning, he immediately goes to the pharmacy to buy a bottle of tonic that helps hair growth, as if baldness is a great misfortune in a person's life. If baldness is indeed a hindrance to a person's appearance, then I think bald people at least have one consolation, because they don't have to bother themselves with frequent haircuts like others.

Art Scene

Reflections After Seeing "Sai Jinhua" 187

— Dian

"Sai Jinhua" has been staged, but until now, no one has given it a correct evaluation. Some people say that this play has lost its theme; others say that this play has even produced two themes; the scriptwriter himself says that this is a "historical allegorical drama." — That is to say: the author stated his attitude in writing this script, focusing not on the theme of the play, but on extracting stories from history and adding "allegory" aimed at reality.

Audiences have a kind of hot

Page 19

and spicy feeling after watching "Sai Jinhua." This "feeling" is not a direct stimulation of the images in the play, but rather a kind of enlightenment as if silently. Therefore, regardless of the shortcomings of the play itself, such as the lack of a clear theme, the lack of concrete characterization, the loose organization, and the unskilled acting, it is only because the "theme" that the play wants to express is being borrowed to express and satirize reality. Therefore, the play itself failed, but the task it wanted to carry out was achieved and successful.

In addition to the above-mentioned shortcomings, the main shortcoming of the play "Sai Jinhua" is that the "dialogue" is divorced from the "plot," but because the scriptwriter is only "using the subject as an excuse," the success of this play is due to several passages of dialogue that are divorced from the plot. It is these few passages of dialogue that are divorced from the plot that can give the audience a kind of silent enlightenment. Therefore, the shortcomings of this play have become the advantages of this play, and the failure of this play is also the success of this play.

The story of "Sai Jinhua" is nothing more than writing about the ups and downs of the life of a famous prostitute, and in the middle, it seems to say a few words of injustice for this "old and unlucky" Sai Jinhua. However, if we look at "Sai Jinhua" with this concept, it will undoubtedly make you feel disappointed. Because Sai Jinhua, who is considered the "protagonist" in this play, has not been able to express the life, personality, and various aspects of this character in a very detailed way; at best, it is only a hasty sketch of this character. Similarly, if you regard "Sai Jinhua" as a historical drama, it will not give you a satisfactory answer, because the historical facts interspersed in it are only some "unofficial histories." Also, if you regard "Sai Jinhua" as a satirical drama, then of course you will not get anything, because the satire of the story of the previous century from the perspective of modern times is equivalent to reasoning with the dead. Therefore, when you watch "Sai Jinhua," you must not forget scriptwriter Xia Yan's words: This is an "allegorical drama." Because if you forget the meaning of "satirizing the past" and "metaphoring the present," it will definitely make you feel empty and disappointed.

The difficult era we are in today is no less than the era of "the Eight-Nation Alliance breaking into Beijing." Sai Jinhua, who lives on Tianqiao in Beiping today, and Sai Jinhua, who lived in the West Empress Dowager's bedroom thirty-six years ago, both saw the power and rampage of the "foreign soldiers" in Beiping. Even if she wants to "be an old commoner who lives in peace" (Sai Jinhua's words in the play), Sai Jinhua will not be able to achieve this wish in this life. Sai Jinhua's sorrow is a reminder of our current difficulties.

At a critical moment in the survival of a nation, even a prostitute who is considered "lower class" still has national thoughts and can eliminate private prejudices (no matter what means she uses) and solve problems that ordinary people cannot solve. Today's traitors are not as good as this frustrated prostitute, and the author's satire is powerful.

These dead past stories are all aimed at the living reality of today. We say that the play "Sai Jinhua" does have two themes: one is the concrete theme in the play, and the other is the abstract theme on the side. This kind of expression will inevitably affect the skills in drama, making the audience unable to obtain a unified and clear understanding, but the environment is the culprit that hinders the progress of art. Although "Sai Jinhua" cannot clearly and boldly explain the current era, its "allegory" does give the audience a great stimulation and impulse.

The performance of "Sai Jinhua" also tells us about the current distress of the Chinese art world: due to the stimulation of reality, they rushed from the palace of art to the crossroads. They have a lot to say, but for various reasons, they cannot say it, and they can only hold it in their throats. However, they know that the era of danger is coming, and they cannot remain silent. They can only disguise themselves and "use the subject as an excuse." This "detour" method will undoubtedly make them commit disloyalty to art itself. The main shortcomings of "Sai Jinhua" are the result of this "detour." In every turbulent era in the past, the progress of art will inevitably encounter this kind of resistance, but from the perspective of the art world itself, today's symbol of distress is also the prelude to the bright future.

This symbol of distress can be said to be a general phenomenon in the art world today. The "allegorical" expression techniques like the play "Sai Jinhua" are the product of this distress. If we can fully utilize this allegorical technique and break out of the atmosphere of distress, it may not be a very important help to the national liberation work of the Chinese nation.

Industry Survey

The Women's Shoe Industry in Little Garden 188

— Bian Beichen

I believe that friends residing in Shanghai, at least, know a little about the women's shoe stores in Little Garden, right?

In fact, the reason why women's shoe stores in Little Garden have such a clear recognition among Shanghai friends is not because they specialize in women's shoes, but because there are so many of them, making it impossible not to pay attention to them.

However, since the opening of the first women's shoe store in Little Garden, it has only been about thirty years. The first one opened was called Taiyuanxiang, followed by Dalu, Sheng Taichang, and Empress, but as of now, there are no fewer than thirty to fifty women's shoe stores in the Xiaohuayuan Zhejiang Road Guangxi Road area!

Before the Shanghai War, their target customers were prostitutes in "book rooms" (brothels). After the failure of "book rooms" after the war, dance halls flourished, and their target customers became dancers, as well as middle and upper-class ladies, because they loved beautiful things. A pair of shoes, when worn by them, would be considered unwearable after at most half a month. As for lower-middle-class women? They are not qualified to patronize! Even if they patronized once for some reason, naturally, they would be reluctant to wear them. Often, a pair of shoes would be worn for more than a year. Therefore, regardless of the boss or the shop assistants, they would not necessarily show any welcome when this type of customer came to patronize their store.

The women's shoe stores in Little Garden before the Shanghai War were in their golden age, but after the end of the war, they had simply reached a period of decline. Now, let me first explain the situation in the women's shoe stores before the Shanghai War:

A double-front women's shoe store with good business averaged three to four hundred yuan in sales per day, while those with poor business averaged one to two hundred yuan; a single-front store with good business also had one hundred and several tens of yuan, while those with poor business had seventy to eighty yuan. The prices of the shoes sold varied, depending on the size of the store. First-class women's shoe stores sold satin embroidered shoes for about two yuan and forty cents per pair, second-class for two yuan and twenty cents, and third-class for two yuan. High-heeled leather shoes had a minimum price of six or seven yuan and a maximum of more than ten yuan. Felt flannel warm shoes, which cost one yuan and thirty or forty cents, would be sold for four yuan. In total, the average profit on shoes was at least 40%. Assuming that this women's shoe store had daily sales of two hundred yuan, then after deducting expenses, it could earn fifty yuan per day. Because it was so easy to make money, the number of women's shoe stores in Little Garden gradually increased.

The loss of revenue of women's shoe stores after the end of the Shanghai War was naturally affected by the economic downturn. Embroidered satin shoes fell from two yuan and forty cents to one yuan (although the cost was slightly lower than before, the difference was still too great). Some stores were selling them for ninety cents, with only a few cents of profit. Selling a pair of high-heeled shoes, on the other hand, would result in a loss of two yuan. Felt shoes also only had thirty or forty cents of profit. However, this was only if the shoes were sold as soon as they were made. If the shoes were left in the store for some time and the style was out of date, even selling them at half price would rarely attract buyers.

Each women's shoe store has more than a hundred styles of women's shoes, each style has seven or eight sizes, and each size has four or five pairs. Therefore, each store has four to five thousand to more than ten thousand pairs of women's shoes. Assuming that each pair costs one yuan, then the capital of a store is four to five thousand yuan or more than ten thousand yuan. But the world now is a modern world. Perhaps something that is considered new this month will be out of date next month. Therefore, women's shoe merchants dare not manufacture various styles of shoes as much as possible, fearing that they will lose money if they cannot sell them all because they are out of date. But the result is that when customers want a certain style of shoe, they are met with a shortage of goods, so the women's shoe industry in Little Garden has failed under this situation!

The shop assistants in the women's shoe stores, who are closely related to the women's shoe merchants, are currently living in even more difficult circumstances. Their treatment, in addition to their wages, includes a 1% commission for each pair of shoes sold. In the past, a shop assistant could usually earn about ten yuan a month in commissions, but now sometimes they can't even earn two or three yuan! At the same time, in order to save expenses, various shoe stores are implementing layoffs and salary reductions. They are worrying about unemployment every day!

Page 21

In the past, during the heyday of women's shoe stores, the shop assistants were very arrogant. Even when a customer had already entered the store, they would not stand up. Now, as long as a passerby glances at the display window, they will come out to greet them. This situation is quite miserable!

At present, many women's shoe stores that have ceased operations have court seals affixed to their doors. A few days ago, the writer happened to pass by Little Garden and discovered that Taiyuanxiang, which had pioneered the women's shoe industry in Little Garden, had also closed down. After returning home, a wave of thoughts flooded my mind! "Is the Shanghai Bund really going to collapse?"

Special Commentary

Siam on the Pacific 189

— He Guangrui

Siam was originally a relatively ancient country in Asia. It had relations with China as early as the Three Kingdoms period. After the Sui and Tang dynasties, it became a vassal state of our country. In the Ming dynasty, it was conquered by Zheng He, and overseas Chinese were able to hold official positions here. In the Qing dynasty, it was destroyed by Burma, and later Hua Zheng Zhao restored the country and called himself the King of Siam. Judging from this historical fact, it can be seen that Siam has a deep relationship with our country. However, during the reign of Emperor Guangxu in the Qing dynasty, the forces of British and French imperialism invaded Siam, plundered its land, and divided its borders into two major spheres of influence. From then on, not only was the deep relationship between Siam and China severed, but also the Chinese compatriots living in Siam were often subjected to unreasonable oppression and exclusion. At the same time, although Siam was able to survive under the contention of the two tigers of Britain and France and was not destroyed, and was able to maintain the signboard of an "independent kingdom" on the surface, in reality, it had already become a semi-colony and one of the main places of competition among the great powers on the Pacific Ocean. Now, due to the development of the world crisis and the increasing seriousness of the problem of re-division of colonies, Siam, as a semi-colony, is of course a place of attention in the great powers' struggle for hegemony on the Pacific Ocean.

The country with the greatest influence in Siam is Britain. Economically speaking, British capital occupies the main monopolistic position here. Whether it is trade, banking, railways, or other capitalist enterprises, it can be said that they are all in the hands of Britain. In order to more concretely understand the problem, let's look at the trade situation between Britain and Siam in 1931 and 1932 during the period of panic (unit: Tai Jial, eleven Tai Jial is one pound)——

According to this fact, it can be seen that Britain occupies an absolutely dominant position in Siam's trade. Siam's main products are rice, teak, and tin, but most of these things are absorbed by Britain. Among them, grain exports to Britain account for 66%, and teak exports to Britain account for 50%. Between 1931 and 1932, Siam exported 11,293,563 Tai Jial of silver overseas, but 10,179,772 Tai Jial of it was exported to Britain. In this way, we can say that the entire economic life of Siam is in the hands of Britain. As for politics, British imperialism also has great control over Siam. It not only uses economic power to influence Siam's politics, but also can directly instigate everything from India, Hong Kong, and Singapore.

However, in recent years, Britain has encountered new powerful enemies in Siam, namely Japan in the Far East. Under the continental and marine policies, Japan is fiercely advancing to the northwest, looking for its "way out" on the mainland of China; on the other hand, it is using Taiwan and the South Seas mandated territories as a basis to develop southward. As a result, the South Seas and Fujian and Guangdong in China have become areas of Japanese activity; Siam is an important area on the Pacific Ocean, and it is a semi-colony that has not yet been swallowed exclusively by a certain "imperialism," which is of course what those who exercise Japanese marine policy are paying attention to. Under this attention, what is first manifested is the dumping of cheap Japanese goods in Siam. According to statistics, in the past year alone, the goods imported from Japan to Siam were worth 40 million yen. It is truly surprising that Siam, a small country with very weak purchasing power, sold so many Japanese goods. At the same time, most of the cotton produced in Siam is also purchased by Japan, which has greatly affected the cotton exported by the United States to the Far East. However, what is particularly noteworthy in Japan's active offensive against Siam is that Japan has obtained the special right to dig the Kra Canal in Siam.

Looking at a map of Siam, you can see that there is a narrow piece of land in Surat Province in Lower Siam, which is located between the South China Sea and the Indian Ocean, bordering the Bay of Bengal to the west and the Gulf of Siam to the east. Following the Malay Peninsula down is Singapore, Britain's economic and military stronghold on the Pacific Ocean. If this place can be navigable, it is truly an essential route for Eurasian transportation. Now, because the Kra Canal has not yet been dug, ships from Europe must detour through Singapore. If the Kra Canal is dug, then the Bay of Bengal and Siam can be directly navigable, shortening the voyage between the Pacific Ocean and the Indian Ocean by three days, which would make Singapore a defunct port, and Kra would replace it and become an essential route for Eurasian transportation. At the same time, after the Kra Canal is dug, Japan can also establish new military bases here to threaten the US Philippines, the British Singapore and Hong Kong, as well as India, Myanmar, and other places, causing serious threats to the United Kingdom and the United States on the Pacific Ocean. Therefore, when the news that Japan had obtained the special right to open the Kra Canal came out, people in London were greatly shocked. Conservative Party member Ryder said in the Lower House: "The matter of Siam opening the Kra Canal must be given great attention, because Japan's participation in this undertaking provides economic assistance." It can be seen how much Britain values this issue.

At the same time, Japan's political activities in Siam are also very active. It not only shouted slogans such as "driving out the oppression of the white ghosts," "liberation of the yellow race," and what "Oriental paradise" to deal with Britain, but also implemented its habitual plan there, organizing "pro-Japanese" groups in an attempt to further develop its power in Siam.

If Japan is a new powerful enemy that Britain has encountered in Siam, then France can be said to be its old enemy. We already know that the first countries to invade Siam were Britain and France, and therefore the first countries to fight in Siam were also them. Looking at it from a geographical perspective, it can be seen that French Annam is on the east side of Siam, British Burma is on the northwest side, and British Malaya is connected to Lower Siam on the south side. In other words, Siam is surrounded by the two major forces of Britain and France. In other words, the forces of Britain and France show an irreconcilable confrontation in Siam. Now, although France cannot deal with the East with great force due to the tense situation in Europe, it has not neglected Siam; at the same time, London has not relaxed its attention to it. In the past, the King of Siam visited Annam and expressed special goodwill to France, which aroused great suspicion in Britain; therefore, after the King returned to Siam, Britain instigated pro-British elements in Siam to protect and expand its rights in Siam. This one thing alone can show the general situation of the infighting between Britain and France in Siam.

British imperialism has already been severely hit by Japan in China's commodity sales and raw material markets, and has been overwhelmed by the United States in the monetary war in the Far East. The reason why it can still occupy an important position in the Pacific Ocean is because the economic, political, and military importance of Hong Kong and Singapore has not been lost. However, Siam has a very close relationship with Singapore and Hong Kong. If its rights in Siam are seized by Japan, then Singapore will become a defunct port, and the security of Hong Kong will be impossible to maintain. Therefore, British imperialism is in danger of being expelled from the Pacific Ocean. Therefore, in the Pacific hegemony war, Britain attaches great importance to Siam; on the one hand, it is actively strengthening the Singapore naval port, preparing for the "final solution" of the Pacific problem - armed resolution, and on the other hand, it is working hard to make the Bangkok (capital of Siam) government completely obey London's control in order to prevent the development of Japanese and even French forces. But in fact, Siam's recent pro-Japanese tendency is very strong, which makes the old British very uneasy.

On the other hand, due to the intensified offensive of the great powers, not only is the country of Siam increasingly losing its independent status, but also the lives of the eight million people of Siam are becoming increasingly impoverished. Therefore, the anti-imperialist and anti-proxy sentiments of the general public in Siam are very high, and unrest is almost everywhere. For this reason, the King of Siam has specially visited British Malaya and French Annam to conclude political and economic reciprocal agreements in an effort to quell the domestic resistance movement.

Now Siam's fate is twofold: either it will become a battlefield for the great powers' Pacific hegemony, or the national liberation movement will succeed and the country will become independent. But no matter what, as long as the current situation in Siam changes, the Pacific situation will also change.

Timely Essay

Busy for Oranges 190

— Lin

Twenty years ago, my hometown still looked like a country bumpkin. There were no roads, no cars, and even fewer dignitaries and their cloud-like followers coming to tour around. Therefore, after the autumn season, almost all the streets and alleys were filled with orange stalls. Speaking of these orange stalls, they can truly be regarded as a work of art: a long plank, leaning against the snow-white high walls of a spacious residence, piled with vermilion-like bright red oranges. The way these oranges are piled is not like the monotonous way Shanghai fruit stores do it, using wooden boxes arranged neatly, which looks very flat. The way they are piled depends on the size of the stall: large ones are often piled into famous mountains and peaks, with rolling hills and towering rocks, looking as if ten thousand mountains are rushing, and startled rocks are bursting; small ones are piled into beautiful pavilions, exquisite pagodas, and so on. In the evening, these peaks and pagodas are lit with small orange lamps. Looking from a distance, the powdered walls reflect a faint red light, and the shadows reflect an undulating, uncertain expanse of vermilion. Late at night, a gentle breeze blows, and the lamp shadows sway, as if these faint lights are listening to the distant barking of dogs, looking somewhat dazed.

Orange lamps, like the stall's furnishings, rely on the intelligence and skill of the orange seller. Some lamps are truly exquisitely made: they select the best-shaped and reddest oranges, dig a small hole in the top, and try to take out the flesh inside little by little, leaving only the entire undamaged orange peel. Then, they carve various patterns of holes in the peel with a knife, sometimes turning up small pieces of the peel to reveal the light real inner peel inside. Only then do they pour in half of a dish of vegetable oil, press two or three stems of lampwick with small coins, and light them up to become a very beautiful orange lamp.

The oranges in my hometown are not sold until the orange peel is completely red. Therefore, there is no such thing as the terrible appearance of the Shanghai orange merchant when the oranges first come out, thinking that the goods are rare and desperately "gouging." When the orange peel is completely red, the orange yield is naturally considerable. At that time, almost all the ships drifting on the river are orange ships. Families with large populations and many children often go directly to the boatmen on the river to buy them, not counting the number, but only how much money per load (that is, one dan). After buying them home, adults and children always eat so much that they can't even eat rice. During this time when oranges fill the market, the flesh is not valuable; what is valuable is the orange peel, the orange seeds, and the fibers attached to the flesh. It is said that these three things can be used as medicine and are my hometown's major export goods every year. Therefore, if you buy ten oranges, eat the flesh, and then take the orange peel to the orange stall, you can exchange it for eight or nine pieces of flesh without peel or fibers. If you don't want to exchange for orange flesh, selling it for cash is also no problem.

The orange yield increases with the winter climate: the colder it gets, the more oranges there are on the market, starting from the end of autumn in the previous year and gradually decreasing until mid-spring of the next year. Therefore, during the New Year, every household, in addition to offering three animals and nine products in front of the ancestors or family gods, also has a plate of heavily stacked bright red oranges and a plate of amber-colored oranges (that is, pomelos). When children come to pay New Year's greetings, in addition to rewarding them with peanuts, sweets, and cash, they are also given a few selected oranges. Oranges, because of their large production, everyone always tries to consume them in various ways. In addition to the several types of consumption mentioned above, everyone also makes them into "orange soup," squeezes them into "orange cakes," and makes them into "orange pastries." It is said that orange soup can sober you up, orange cakes can cure tuberculosis, and orange pastries can "regulate qi," specializing in treating stomach pain. I have not tested whether these have these effects. No matter what Chinese people do, they always have to find a legitimate excuse. In addition, if you have a cough, you dig a hole in the top of the orange, pour in a little sesame oil, and put it on the fire to bake. When the orange is roasted until it is charred and the flesh is completely permeated with sesame oil, it is peeled off and eaten. It is said that this is also a good "simple prescription."

My hometown has more than seventy counties, and almost every county produces oranges, largely because the climate and soil throughout the province are similar. An orange grove often occupies two or three hundred li. I heard that anyone is very free to go to the grove to play and admire, and is never subject to any restrictions, because according to the rules of the grove, tourists are allowed to pick and eat, but they cannot take them away. This is truly the difference between a big family and a small family compared to the laws of various American countries, which stipulate that the orchard owner can shoot to death passers-by who pick fruit! In my hometown, there is also a rule that if oranges protrude from the walls of the grove, even if passers-by want to pick them and take them away, the grove owner cannot interfere.

The planting of oranges is very simple. As long as the climate and soil are suitable, putting down the seeds (that is, orange seeds) will always allow them to grow. However, from the time the seeds are put in to the time the fruit is produced, it takes a long time. Therefore, there is a saying in my hometown: "Peaches take three years, plums take four years, and oranges take eight years." In short, oranges are a product of the temperate zone. The warmer the climate, the faster they grow and the better the quality of the fruit. In countries such as Italy, orange trees can be expected to bear fruit in three to five years, and the fruit produced is much sweeter than those in my hometown.

Twenty years ago, every winter, we were busy with oranges, making lamps, pressing cakes, and boiling sugar, without a moment of peace. This winter, twenty years later, when I went home, I could no longer see any of this phenomenon. The streets already had Shanghai-style fruit stores, and what they sold were actually large boxes of "Yantai apples," "American oranges," "Siamese pomelos," "American grapes"...! The oranges produced in my hometown, like those in fruit stores in Shanghai, were placed on small stalls in front of the store along with those unpopular mountain potatoes and radish heads! To see oranges alone, unless in the hands of peddlers who scream hoarsely late at night, selling along the streets, these are specially sold to laborers who rest at night to relieve the scorched feeling after smoking opium.
